               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cphc202400832-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/78afca40-5957-4692-a452-d2efcbd47d26/cphc202400832-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/78afca40-5957-4692-a452-d2efcbd47d26/cphc202400832-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f88c618d-0cef-48a0-8f74-f6b45bb6b990/cphc202400832-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/78afca40-5957-4692-a452-d2efcbd47d26/cphc202400832-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cphc202400832-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcphc.202400832" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Lattice parameters of the hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i> phase, volume and weight fractions of both hexagonal and monoclinic phases as a function of temperature.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Considering the phase evolution of P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> during electrochemical charge-discharge, FigureS6 shows the points of extraction, Rietveld-refined fits, and phase composition as a function of the state of charge. FigureS7 shows zoomed regions of these fits and FiguresS8-S10 show the refined lattice parameters and volume. Note the cycled electrodes were extracted on the 2<sup>nd</sup> cycle. The electrode remains wholly hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> or P2 at the partially charged (PC), fully charged (FC), partially discharged (PD) and as expected at the non-cycled (NC) sample. At the discharged states where Na is fully inserted, there are more phases present. In the 1<sup>st</sup> discharged state (FD) a monoclinic phase was found to coexist with orthorhombic phases and at the 2<sup>nd</sup> discharged state (FD_R) orthorhombic, hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> and monoclinic phases co-exist. The transition to an orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> phase during the discharging process from the hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase has been reported previously.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0006_R_d14778620e1500" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Angewandte Chemie">6</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>It is worthwhile to compare this evolution with the evolution found in the literature, TableS3 shows selected studies with the phases reported and where possible lattice parameters and Na content noted. The evolution of volume and lattice parameters of all phases derived from this study are shown in TableS4. The observed hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> or P2 lattice parameters of the NC, PC, FC and PD samples closely align with those reported in the literature.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0005_R_d14778620e1510" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Energy Environ. Sci.">5</a>, <a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0006_R_d14778620e1510" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Angewandte Chemie">6</a>, <a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0014_R_d14778620e1510" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Inorg. Chem.">14</a></sup></span> Interestingly, the hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase is not observed in sample FD.</p>
         
         <p>FigureS8 shows that the hexagonal <i>P6<sub>3</sub>/mmc</i> phase volume of the NC sample is comparatively higher than the FC electrode; however, it is lower than PC and PD samples. The highest volume is shown by sample FD_R among all analysed samples. A similar trend was observed in <i>a</i> lattice parameter evolution while the <i>c</i> lattice parameter shows the opposite behaviour. The <i>c</i> lattice parameter is related to the interplanar distance between the transition metal oxide layers.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0006_R_d14778620e1533" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Angewandte Chemie">6</a>, <a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0037_R_d14778620e1533" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Nat Commun">37</a></sup></span> The NC sample shows a comparatively lower <i>c</i> lattice parameter compared to the FC sample and this correlates with the literature.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0006_R_d14778620e1539" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Angewandte Chemie">6</a></sup></span> As Na is removed from the lattice, there is significant OO interaction between the transition metal oxide layers which results in an expansion of the <i>c</i> lattice parameter. The NC <i>c</i> lattice parameter is larger than the PC and PD electrodes likely indicating a larger amount of Na in the electrodes. The smallest <i>c</i> lattice parameter is observed in the FD_R electrode which correlates to the highest Na content. Overall, at the higher Na content states a contraction of the <i>c</i> lattice parameter was observed.</p>
         
         <p>At the discharge states, the presence of multiple phases are clearly noted and this posed a challenge for phase identification. Distinguishing the most probable phase among the variety of phases required careful analysis. Therefore, various structural models and combinations of structural models were explored to determine or estimate the most probable structures. Based on the combination of visual fitting, i.e., peak mis-match, and statistical results from Rietveld analysis, as shown in TablesS5 and S6, the structural models that best fit the data are used at these states. Note, that a similar approach was applied during the thermal analysis (discussed below).</p>
         
         <p>The FD_R electrode is of interest as there is a mixture of phases and the hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase shows the largest volume (3.0% larger than the NC) and smallest <i>c</i> lattice parameter (1.8% smaller than the NC). This is likely the most Na-rich hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase in this work. Note, previous work shows an 11.2% volume change between x =0.327 and 0.998 in Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0038_R_d14778620e1572" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Nat. Commun.">38</a></sup></span> The reported lattice parameters for the orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> phase<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0029_R_d14778620e1577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angewandte Chemie">29</a></sup></span> and the monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> phase<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0036_R_d14778620e1585" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - J Solid State Chem">36</a></sup></span> are similar to the corresponding parameters observed in samples FD and FD_R. Note, the differing Na content in these phases may account for some differences in the lattice parameters. In the literature, the commonly reported phase at the higher Na content, e.g., from x =0.74 to 0.96,<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0029_R_d14778620e1588" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angewandte Chemie">29</a></sup></span> is orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> or P2 based on XRD<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0006_R_d14778620e1593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Angewandte Chemie">6</a>, <a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0024_R_d14778620e1593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Commun.">24</a>, <a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0029_R_d14778620e1593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angewandte Chemie">29</a>, <a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0039_R_d14778620e1593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Energy Storage Mater.">39</a></sup></span> and NMR<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0029_R_d14778620e1597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angewandte Chemie">29</a></sup></span> studies. The occurrence of the orthorhombic phase was also documented at x &lt;0.67<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0006_R_d14778620e1600" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Angewandte Chemie">6</a></sup></span> and x &lt;0.715<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0038_R_d14778620e1603" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Nat. Commun.">38</a></sup></span> in some work. The differences in the volume of the orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> phases at the discharged states was only 0.16%.</p>
         
         <p>There is a variety of reported phase transitions during electrochemical cycling for nominally P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>. In an <i>insitu</i> study of P2 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> five distinct hexagonal phases all adopting <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> could be identified during the cycling process.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0014_R_d14778620e1627" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Inorg. Chem.">14</a></sup></span> NMR work probing the <sup>23</sup>Na chemical shift suggests the presence of a monoclinic phase during the discharge step between 0.45 &lt; x &lt;0.68 and in the 2<sup>nd</sup> charge cycle between 0.76 &lt; x &lt;0.55 and this is supported by XRD studies.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0029_R_d14778620e1635" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angewandte Chemie">29</a></sup></span> Samples FD and FD_R appear to exhibit a monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> phase with weight fractions of 0.16(1) and 0.24(1), respectively. The monoclinic phase lattice parameters are higher in the FD_R sample compared to the FD sample (FigureS10).</p>
         
         <p>Therefore, the overall phase evolution at room temperature appears to show orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> and monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> at FD first discharge, hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase at PC, FC and PD stages, and then a combination of hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i>, orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i>, and monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> in the FD_R stage (FigureS9).</p>
         
         <p>It is interesting to understand and compare the thermal evolution of the samples extracted at various states of charge and the as-synthesized powder. Figure<a href="#cphc202400832-fig-0003">3</a> shows the phase evolution as a function of temperature and state of charge. These were determined using sequential Rietveld analysis with various structural models. Each phase was modelled using a range of different potential structures and the model with the best fit is presented. These experiments are conducted in a quartz capillary with a static Ar atmosphere. It should be noted that all electrodes contain polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) and carbon black, and previous work has shown that PVDF melts around 450C<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0040_R_d14778620e1675" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Nanomaterials">40</a></sup></span> see TGA data in FigureS12 of ref.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0041_R_d14778620e1678" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Dalton Transactions">41</a></sup></span> Work has also shown the impact of binder on the thermal evolution on active materials. Furthermore, it should be noted that the electrodes are composites, during electrochemical processes surface layers do form and during electrode extraction, washing and drying, salts derived from the electrolyte can remain on the electrodes. Considering the quantity of these components and their crystallinity, in a diffraction pattern the crystalline active material signal dominates. Therefore, the thermal evolution is a complex interaction of these species where the crystalline component from the active material dominates as does its evolution. The sequence of reactions are impacted by the components, e.g., the melting of PVDF or the reaction with carbon black and potential formation of reductive gases such as CO<sub>2</sub>.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cphc202400832-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/63737be5-301d-44a2-90e1-5b1e8f9dc517/cphc202400832-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/63737be5-301d-44a2-90e1-5b1e8f9dc517/cphc202400832-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1941a6bc-8cd3-47ba-b0b9-1c507d590a76/cphc202400832-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/63737be5-301d-44a2-90e1-5b1e8f9dc517/cphc202400832-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cphc202400832-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcphc.202400832" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>(a) Thermal evolution of Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> at various states of charge. Weight fractions are derived from Rietveld analysis using a variety of structural models. (b) The contour plots show the evolution of a selected 2 range ( =0.68729(1)).</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>For these refinements, the background, weight fraction and lattice parameters were refined. The profile parameters were kept constant wherever possible. For each phase, crystal size and strain terms were determined from a single refinement and subsequently fixed. Atomic parameters were kept at the values reported in the Inorganic Crystal Structure Database (ICSD)<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0042_R_d14778620e1713" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Crystallography Reviews">42</a></sup></span> as the complexity in the phases present didn't allow sufficient reliability to refine these parameters.</p>
         
         <p>One of the key challenges in this work was identifying the phases around 200350C in each case and phases below 350C for the discharged sample. In order to identify the phases present, e.g., monoclinic, hexagonal, orthorhombic, temperatures were selected which featured the highest weight fraction of each phase. For example, in the NC sample at 400C the phase termed secondary had the highest intensity. This phase was initially modelled with a secondary P2 (hexagonal, <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i>)<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0029_R_d14778620e1725" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angewandte Chemie">29</a></sup></span> or P2 (orthorhombic, <i>Cmcm</i>) phase, in addition to the original P2 phase and NaF and Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> present at this temperature. The phases for Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> were typically found in the ICSD and are shown in Tables<a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#cphc202400832-tbl-0001">1</a> and S3. Inspecting the quality of the refinements, <i>i.e</i>., peak matching, and statistics of the fit, either the hexagonal or the orthorhombic phase obtained good quality fits, see TableS8. Sequential refinements were typically undertaken using both structural models, however, the cases presented here were on the best-fit model. In some cases, clear peaks can be identified for certain structural models.</p>
         
         <p>Figure<a href="#cphc202400832-fig-0003">3a</a> shows that very similar phases are formed across the electrochemical series as a function of temperature with the presence of a secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> (except in FD), NaF, Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> and MnO observed in all cases. In Figure<a href="#cphc202400832-fig-0004">4b</a>, the contour plots depict the evolution of the (002) reflection for the hexagonal phases, and the (001) reflection for the monoclinic phase between 30C and 500C. All samples transform into tetragonal Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> followed by cubic MnO and a persistent NaF phase is formed in conjunction. This implies that the environment is reducing as the Mn oxidation state evolves from a mix of Mn<sup>3+/4+</sup> in the electrodes to 2<sup>+</sup>/3<sup>+</sup> in Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> and 2<sup>+</sup> in MnO. This could be a result of the carbon components and potentially the formation of reducing gases such as CO<sub>2</sub> with thermal treatments.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cphc202400832-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/766e1daa-2171-47da-a550-17ca8212d981/cphc202400832-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/766e1daa-2171-47da-a550-17ca8212d981/cphc202400832-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/b23b1db0-40b3-4f2a-be14-aafd124ca926/cphc202400832-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/766e1daa-2171-47da-a550-17ca8212d981/cphc202400832-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cphc202400832-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcphc.202400832" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Lattice parameters and volume evolution of the two hexagonal P6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i> phases found between 30500C.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The PC and PD states of charge are expected to have similar sodium concentrations and show similar phase compositions to the NC electrode. These and the charged (Na-poor) FC electrode show the same phase transitions, from the hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> P2 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> to a secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> P2 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and NaF followed by Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> and MnO. PD and PC show an additional phase, monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> O3 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> around 500C (shown as a star symbol in Figure<a href="#cphc202400832-fig-0003">3a</a>). The onset of these transitions and the stability range of the phases vary depending on the state of charge.</p>
         
         <p>In the case of FD or the discharged state (Na-rich), this begins as orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> P2 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> at room temperature with a residual amount of monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> O3 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> (see FigureS11), then transforms to a secondary orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> P2 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> phase with temperature. As an example, a statistical comparison is shown in TableS8, aiming to establish whether the secondary phase was orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> or hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> at 150C. This then transforms to tetragonal Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>, cubic NaF and cubic MnO with further heating. Typically, there is a much more complex sequence of phase transitions, especially at lower temperatures, in this Na-rich sample compared to the other lower Na-content state samples.</p>
         
         <p>Furthermore, the formation of the secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase in the FC sample occurs at a much lower temperature than the formation of the secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase in other samples. Overall, it is interesting to note that the states of charge or Na-content in the Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> electrode do not have a large impact on the thermal phase evolution as the secondary Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> (either hexagonal or orthorhombic), NaF, Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> and MnO are formed in every case probed here. Selected Rietveld refinements of structural models to the XRD data that depict the thermal evolution of each sample are shown in FigureS13.</p>
         
         <p>The original hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> to secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> transition is observed at 200C for FC, 250C for NC and PD and 300C for PC. The secondary hexagonal phase becomes the predominant phase between 300C to 350C for FC, 350C to 400C for NC, PC and 300C to 400C for PD. Tetragonal Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> first emerges at 350C in NC, FC and PD and 400C in PC and becomes the predominant phase between 450C and 600C in NC, PC and PD and 400C to 550C in FC. In all samples cubic MnO is clearly observed at 550C and tetragonal Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> disappears after 650C. In FD, the monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> remains until 500C, the secondary orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> forms at 150C and dominates between 200C and 350C and higher temperature evolution follows the other samples. NaF appears between 200350C in all cases.</p>
         
         <p>The lattice parameter and volume evolution as a function of the state of charge and temperature were evaluated. Figure<a href="#cphc202400832-fig-0004">4</a> shows the lattice parameter evolution of both hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> phases (in NC, PC, FC and PD). The original hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> <i>c</i> lattice parameters overall increase, while the <i>a</i> lattice parameter increases to 200C for NC and FC and decreases for PC and PD. After 200C the <i>a</i> lattice parameter decreases for all samples. The volume also shows a change around 200C, with an increase in volume below this temperature and a decrease above it in all cases. Note at higher temperatures the errors become larger as the weight fraction of this phase decreases.</p>
         
         <p>The change in the <i>a</i> lattice parameter and volume around 200C can be caused by a number of factors including the inherent thermal expansion/contraction of this phase, the onset of a phase transition, e.g., formation of the secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase, and/or a change in the sodium concentration of this phase. Typically, during electrochemical discharge, sodium extraction, from P2-type materials, results in an expansion of the <i>c</i> lattice parameter (OO repulsion from adjacent <i>TM</i>O<sub>6</sub> layers) and a contraction of the <i>a</i> lattice parameter (increase in TM oxidation state, reducing <i>TM</i>-O bond lengths). The observed thermal evolution particularly after 200C is reminiscent of this behaviour, particularly in the primary hexagonal phase.</p>
         
         <p>The secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i> phase is found between 200500C. Similar lattice parameters are observed across these samples, e.g., at 400C, suggesting that similar compositions and structures are being formed in each case. The secondary hexagonal phase shows a general decrease in the <i>c</i> lattice parameters and relatively stable <i>a</i> lattice parameters and overall volume. FD was noted earlier to feature a more complex phase evolution than the other samples. The orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> phase (Figure<a href="#cphc202400832-fig-0005">5</a>) that is present at room temperature, shows an increase in the <i>b</i> and <i>c</i> lattice parameters and volume and a decrease in the <i>a</i> lattice parameter, and disappears around 250C. The secondary orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> phase that appears at 150C shows an initial decrease in the <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> lattice parameters and volume and an increase in the <i>c</i> lattice parameter. After 250C, when the original <i>Cmcm</i> phase disappears, the <i>b</i> lattice parameter and volume begin to increase while <i>a</i> remains relatively stable and <i>c</i> goes through a maximum and begins to decrease. Furthermore, in FD a small but persistent monoclinic <i>C2/m</i> phase could be modelled from room temperature to 500C, with only small variations in lattice parameters and volume (FigureS11). In all the samples the cubic <i>Fm</i>-3<i>m</i> NaF phase (FigureS12) appears between 200C350C and shows linear expansion after 500C with a coefficient of thermal expansion of 8.72(1)10<sup>5</sup>K<sup>1</sup>.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cphc202400832-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5a796126-8f81-4566-8e59-2aefc124a317/cphc202400832-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/5a796126-8f81-4566-8e59-2aefc124a317/cphc202400832-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f7432a09-c55e-422b-ba62-ac47119442c7/cphc202400832-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5a796126-8f81-4566-8e59-2aefc124a317/cphc202400832-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cphc202400832-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcphc.202400832" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Lattice parameters and volume evolution of the orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> phase(s), labelled FD_1 and FD_2 found between 30400C in sample FD.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Speculatively, the formation of the NaF can be attributed to the melting of PVDF around 450C and reaction of F with Na from Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, most likely reacting or leaching from the surface of the Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> particles. This in turn generates Na-deficient regions which transform to MnO<sub>x</sub>. The carbon from the carbon black component generates the reducing conditions necessary to drive the reaction to Mn<sup>4+</sup>. Alternatively, NaF can be present in the cathode electrolyte interphase (CEI) after electrochemical processes and remain on the electrode surface as nanosized components.<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0043_R_d14778620e2091" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Small Methods">43</a></sup></span> These components can growth, removing Na and F from the Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and PVDF, respectively which in turn results in the formation of MnO<sub>x</sub>. It should be noted that the experiments were undertaken in a sealed quartz capillary where the capillary was sealed in an Ar environment, which is slightly reducing.</p>
         
         <p>The occurrence of NaF at relatively low temperatures in the non-cycled electrode suggests a reaction between the binder (PVDF) and Na from Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>. Moreover, in the cycled extracted electrodes the NaF may crystallise from the CEI, i.e., a component in the CEI, or derive from a reaction with any residual electrolyte salts on the electrode or react with the binder. The correlation between NaF formation and the reduction in weight fraction of the original hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase also provides evidence for such a reaction. Finally, the secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phases noted in all the samples (with the exception of FD) exhibit a larger <i>c</i> lattice parameter than the original hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase, consistent with a smaller concentration of Na in the Na layers of the P2 type Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> structure.</p>
         
         <p>Figure<a href="#cphc202400832-fig-0006">6</a> shows the lattice and volume evolution of the tetragonal Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> and cubic MnO phases. At 350 and 400C, Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> appears to show a small spread in the lattice parameters and volume depending on the state of charge. The difference may indicate a small solid solution where Na is present in the structure. However, it should be noted that at 350C in particular, the weight fraction of Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> are quite low and this is evident in the larger error bars on the lattice parameters. Overall, Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> and MnO<sub>2</sub> are consistently formed across the samples and similar to NaF from 450C show relatively linear thermal expansion. The thermal expansion coefficient for Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> between 400 to 650C is 2.47(8)10<sup>5</sup>K<sup>1</sup> and for MnO between 550 to 750C is 4.29(2)10<sup>5</sup>K<sup>1</sup>. MnO and NaF remain after cooling.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cphc202400832-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/30c039b1-973a-4e72-bfbe-d4eaad2282a6/cphc202400832-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/30c039b1-973a-4e72-bfbe-d4eaad2282a6/cphc202400832-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/93997727-c9fb-47af-a470-857b83bb0b78/cphc202400832-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/30c039b1-973a-4e72-bfbe-d4eaad2282a6/cphc202400832-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cphc202400832-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcphc.202400832" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>The (a) volume evolution of the Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> and MnO phases and (b-c) the volume and lattice parameter evolution of Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cphc202400832-sec-0003">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cphc202400832-sec-0003-title"> Conclusions</h2>
         
         <p>This work shows the electrochemical and thermal evolution of P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> electrodes. P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> heated under an open N<sub>2</sub> environment forms a secondary monoclinic <i>C</i>2/<i>m</i> phase, from about 450C and grows to about 52% at 750C. P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> electrodes, with carbon black and PVDF, and electrochemically cycled variants show very similar high-temperature phase evolution to each other when heated in sealed Ar-filled quartz capillaries. They all transform into NaF, Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> followed by MnO demonstrating a reduction in the Mn oxidation state and a disappearance of crystalline Na-containing layered components. All extracted electrodes, besides the discharged (Na-inserted) state, show an evolution from the original hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> P2 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> to a secondary hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> P2 Na<sub>x</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> phases prior to the appearance of Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>. The discharged states, show a mix of phases at room temperature, a combination of orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> and monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> at both discharge states and re-emergence of the hexagonal <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub><i>/mmc</i> phase at the 2<sup>nd</sup> discharge state. The thermal evolution of the first discharged state begins with the orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> and monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> phases, with the monoclinic <i>C</i>2<i>/m</i> phase remaining until 500C, and the orthorhombic <i>Cmcm</i> phase transforming into a second orthorhombic phase around 150C before the sample forms NaF and Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>. NaF forms between 200-350C in all cases. Overall, these results indicate that irrespective of state of charge the thermal phase evolution is very similar under the conditions used. Future work, investigating different external conditions, e.g., evolution under O<sub>2</sub>, or with different types of binders may shed light on the stability and accessibility of other phases in this and related systems.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cphc202400832-sec-0004">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cphc202400832-sec-0004-title"> Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <p>To synthesize P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (Sigma-Aldrich, 99%) and MnCO<sub>3</sub> (Fisher, 99%) were ground using a mortar and pestle in a stoichiometric ratio. A Retsch planetary ball mill (400rpm for 2hours) was used to further mix the compound. This compound was subsequently calcinated at 650C for 15h, furnace cooled to 530C before being quenched to room temperature and stored in an Ar-filled glovebox. Scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) analyses were conducted using a Hitachi TM4000Plus electron microscope. To identify the phase, laboratory XRD analysis was carried out on a Malvern Panalyical MPD with Cu K radiation (=1.5418) and/or Empyrean 2 with Co K radiation (=1.7902).</p>
         
         <p>Laboratory variable temperature XRD experiments were performed on as-prepared powders using the Malvern Panalytical Empyrean 1 equipped with a heating stage and Cu K <span style="text-decoration:underline">radiation</span> (=1.5418)<span style="text-decoration:underline">. D</span>ata were collected at RT, 50C, followed by increments of 50C to 750C with a 50Cmin<sup>1</sup> ramp-up rate under a N<sub>2</sub> atmosphere.</p>
         
         <p>Electrodes were prepared by mixing active material (P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>) with carbon black as the conductive agent and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) as the binder in an 80:10:10 weight ratio. The slurry of the mixture was made using N-methyl pyrrolidone (NMP) as the solvent. Next, the mixture was coated onto aluminium foil and dried at 100C for 18h in a vacuum oven. Electrodes of 12mm diameter were punched out of the coated foil and pressed under a load of 100kN and dried again before transfer to the glovebox. The electrochemical performance of P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> was evaluated using coin cells assembled in an Ar-filled glovebox. Metallic sodium was used as the negative electrode and glass fibre separators were used. A solution of 0.6M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in ethylene carbonate, propyl carbonate, and fluoroethylene carbonate (EC/PC/FEC 49:49:2vol %) was used as the electrolyte.</p>
         
         <p>Galvanostatic cycling for the cells was performed between 41.5V for P2 Na<sub>2/3</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> on a Landt battery tester. Charge-discharge cycles were typically undertaken with a current density of 20mAg<sup>1</sup> for charge and 10mAg<sup>1</sup> for discharge. To extract the cathodes at different states of charge in their second cycle for thermal studies, the first cycle was conducted with a charging rate of 40mAg<sup>1</sup> and a discharging rate of 10mAg<sup>1</sup>. Subsequently, the second cycle involved a charging rate of 20mAg<sup>1</sup> and a discharging rate of 10mAg<sup>1</sup>. Cells were cycled to achieve fully discharged (1<sup>st</sup> discharged state), partially charged, fully charged, partially discharged, and another fully discharged state (2<sup>nd</sup> discharged state). All the cells were cycled at room temperature.</p>
         
         <p>For ex-situ variable temperature synchrotron XRD experiments, the non-cycled and other extracted electrodes from coin cells were washed with dimethyl carbonate (DMC) and dried inside the glovebox. Electrode materials were then scraped from the Al current collector, ground and filled into 0.5mm quartz capillaries, and sealed inside the glovebox. XRD data were collected on the powder diffraction beamline at the Australian Synchrotron using a wavelength of 0.68729(1). The wavelength was determined by performing Rietveld analysis using XRD data on a NIST LaB<sub>6</sub> reference material collected at the start of the beamtime. Sample data were collected at RT, 50C, followed by increments of 50C to 750C with a 10Cmin<sup>1</sup> ramp rate using an FMB Oxford hot air blower. In all cases, two additional data sets were collected during the cooling process at 200 C and 30C.</p>
         
         <p>Rietveld refinements were carried out using the GSASII software package<span><sup><a href="#cphc202400832-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cphc202400832-bib-0044_R_d14778620e2370" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - J Appl. Crystallogr.">44</a></sup></span>. Background, profile, weight fractions, lattice and in some cases selected atomic parameters and preferred orientation terms (spherical harmonics) were refined. Various parameters were optimised in a systematic approach and attempts were made to keep parameters consistent across the compositional and thermal series wherever possible.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cphc202400832-sec-0005-title"> Acknowledgments</h2>
